     - **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Marafiq", "Trine University", "Sensetime", "Google", "Envision", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy")

     - **System or technology names** (e.g., "financial data storage system", "deep learning models", "computer vision")
   - Replace each PII element with a **contextually appropriate placeholder**, such as:
     - [Recipient Name] for individual names
     - [Company Name] for organizations or companies
     - [Customer Name] for customer or client names
     - [University Name] for educational institutions
     - [Product Name] for products or technical terms
     - [City Name] for locations
     - [Job Title] for roles or positions
     - [System Name] for specific systems or technologies

2. **Preservation of Original Structure and Meaning**:
   - Maintain the **original structure** of the input, including:
     - Line breaks
     - Markdown formatting (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists)
     - Punctuation and syntax
   - Do **not alter the intent or meaning** of the original query, even if PII is removed or replaced.
   - Ensure that **instructions, questions, and statements** are preserved in their original form.

3. **Consistency and Contextual Appropriateness**:
   - Use **consistent placeholders** for each type of PII. For example, do not use [Recipient Name] for both a customer and a company unless the context clearly indicates otherwise.
   - Avoid **reusing the same placeholder** for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the entity type.

4. **Avoiding PII Leakage**:
   - Ensure that **no PII remains** in the rewritten query.
   - Double-check for any **accidental retention** of PII, even in the form of partial names, numbers, or acronyms.
   - Replace **brand-specific or proprietary terms** (e.g., "Stan Store", "Marafiq", "Sensetime") with generic placeholders.

5. **Technical and Domain-Specific Considerations**:
   - Be **especially cautious with technical or product-specific terms**, even if they are not full names, as they may be PII in the context of the query.
   - For **job titles or roles**, use [Job Title] as the placeholder.
   - For **system names or technologies**, use [System Name] or [Product Name] as appropriate.
   - If the input contains **mixed content types** (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve the structure in the rewritten output.

6. **Generalizable Strategy**:
   - Use a **systematic approach** to identify and replace PII by scanning the text for any identifiable names, organizations, or terms that could be used to trace back to real-world entities.
   - Apply a **placeholder mapping** strategy where each identified PII is mapped to a generic placeholder based on its type and context.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is **grammatically correct, clear, and suitable** for downstream processing or analysis.

7. **Final Review**:
   - Review the rewritten query to ensure **no PII leakage** and that all placeholders are **used consistently and appropriately**.
   - Ensure that the **original intent, meaning, and structure** of the query are preserved.

### Task Description
You will be provided with a text input that may contain various types of PII, including:
- **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Ahmad", "Radwa", "Engr. Abdulmazid")
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Marafiq", "Trine University", "Sensetime", "Google")
- **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "common area meter", "deep learning models", "financial data storage system")
- **Job titles or roles** (e.g., "software engineer", "researcher", "quant developer")
- **Customer names or identifiers** (e.g., "radwa 08", "tohama 0715")
- **University or educational institution names** (e.g., "Peking University", "Trine University")
- **Specific locations or cities** (e.g., "Arlington", "Beijing")
- **Other entities that could identify real-world individuals or organizations**

### Instructions
1. **Identify and Replace PII**: Replace all instances of PII with appropriate generic placeholders such as:
   - [Recipient Name] for names of individuals
   - [Company Name] for company or organization names
   - [Customer Name] for customer or client names
   - [University Name] for educational institutions
   - [Product Name] for products or technical systems
   - [Job Title] for job roles
   - [City Name] for locations
   - [Technical Field] for technical areas or applications
   - [System or Technology] for specific systems or technologies
   - [Your Name] for the sender's name (if present)

2. **Preserve Structure and Meaning**: Maintain the original structure, formatting, and intent of the input, including:
   - Line breaks and markdown (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists)
   - Lists, bullet points, and other formatting elements
   - Questions, instructions, and other content types
   - Grammatical correctness and clarity

3. **Avoid PII Leakage**: Ensure that no PII from the original text appears in the anonymized output. This includes:
   - Avoiding the use of any real-world names, company names, or technical terms
   - Ensuring that placeholders are used consistently and appropriately
   - Avoiding the reuse of the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the entity type

4. **Contextual Appropriateness**: Use placeholders that are contextually relevant to the type of PII being replaced. For example:
   - Use [Recipient Name] for names of individuals addressed in the text
   - Use [Company Name] for names of companies or organizations
   - Use [Product Name] for specific product or technical terms
   - Use [Platform Name] for specific platform names (e.g., "Stan Store")

5. **Consistency and Precision**: Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently throughout the text. For example, if "Trine University" is replaced with [University Name], then all instances of "Trine University" must be replaced with [University Name].

6. **Avoid Assumptions**: Do not infer the intent of the user beyond what is explicitly stated in the query. Stick strictly to the task of anonymization and do not alter the original meaning or intent of the text.

7. **Use Generalizable Strategies**: Apply a generalizable strategy for identifying and replacing PII, such as:
   - Scanning for proper nouns, company names, and technical terms
   - Replacing them with the most appropriate placeholder based on context
   - Ensuring that the anonymized text is suitable for downstream processing, such as data analysis, compliance, or customer support

### Examples of Expected Output
- Input: "I am excited to apply for the Master of Science in Information Studies program at Trine University."
- Output: "I am excited to apply for the Master of Science in Information Studies program at [University Name]."

- Input: "Dear Engr. Abdulmazid, I like to inform you that radwa 08 tohama 0715 common area meter there is no power supply as per Marafiq."
- Output: "Dear Engr. [Recipient Name], I like to inform you that [Customer Name] 08 [Customer Name] 0715 common area meter there is no power supply as per [Company Name]."

- Input: "Good evening Ahmad, I hope you had a great week."
- Output: "Good evening [Recipient Name], I hope you had a great week."

- No PII remains in the text
- Placeholders are used consistently and appropriately
- The original structure, intent, and meaning of the text are preserved
- The output is grammatically correct and clear

Iteration 4 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize Text by Removing and Replacing Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

## Task Description

You are tasked with anonymizing a given text by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) and replacing it with consistent, contextually appropriate generic placeholders. This includes, but is not limited to, names of individuals, company or organization names, product or technical terms, customer names, city names, and any other specific entities that could identify real-world individuals, organizations, or entities.

The goal is to ensure that the anonymized text maintains the **original intent, structure, and meaning** of the input while ensuring **no PII leakage** occurs. The output must be suitable for downstream processing, such as in customer support, compliance, data analysis, or other privacy-preserving scenarios.

## Detailed Instructions

### 1. Identify and Replace PII
- **Individual Names**: Replace names like "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim", etc., with **[Recipient Name]** or **[Name]**, depending on context.
- **Company/Organization Names**: Replace names like "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision", etc., with **[Company Name]**.
- **Product or Technical Terms**: Replace terms like "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS", etc., with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]**, depending on context.
- **Customer Names**: Replace names like "radwa", "tohama", etc., with **[Customer Name]**.
- **City Names**: Replace city names like "Arlington" with **[City Name]**.
- **Job Titles or Roles**: Replace titles like "quant developer", "software engineer", "researcher", etc., with **[Job Title]** or **[Role]**.
- **System or Platform Names**: Replace names like "Stan Store" with **[Platform Name]** or **[System Name]**.

### 2. Maintain Original Structure and Context
- **Preserve formatting**: Maintain lists, line breaks, markdown elements like `<br/>`, and numbered lists.
- **Preserve intent and meaning**: Do not alter the original intent or meaning of the query, even if it requires careful placeholder selection.
- **Maintain grammatical correctness and clarity**: Ensure that the anonymized text is grammatically correct and clear in meaning.

### 3. Avoid PII Leakage
- Ensure that no original PII remains in the output.
- Use consistent placeholders throughout the text for the same type of PII.
- Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.

### 4. Special Considerations
- **Technical Terms**: Even if a term is not a full name, if it is brand-specific or proprietary (e.g., "EVBP", "PA12"), it should be anonymized with a placeholder like **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]**.
- **Mixed Content Types**: If the input contains a mix of content types (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the output.
- **Avoid Assumptions**: Do not infer or assume the user’s intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.

### 5. Quality and Consistency
- Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- Review the anonymized output to confirm that it is free of PII leakage and maintains the original meaning and structure.

## Examples of Proper Placeholder Usage

| Original Text                          | Anonymized Text                                 |
|----------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------|
| "I work at Google."                    | "I work at [Company Name]."                      |
| "I trained deep learning models at Sensetime." | "I trained deep learning models at [Company Name]." |
| "radwa 08 tohama 0715"                | "[Customer Name] 08 [Customer Name] 0715"       |
| "I am excited to join Trine University." | "I am excited to join [University Name]."       |

## Final Review

- No PII remains in the output.
- Placeholders are used consistently and contextually.
- The anonymized text is grammatically correct and preserves the original intent and structure.

Iteration 6 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning and intent.

Specific instructions and considerations:

1. **PII Identification**: Identify and anonymize all PII, including but not limited to:
   - Full names (e.g., "Erik", "Seema Taneja")
   - Addresses (e.g., "Name, Number and street name, Town or City, County, Postcode")
   - Company or organization names (e.g., "PIDILITE", "MGS HOSPITAL", "AKHIL BHARTIYA NATRA SANG", "SWAYAM TRUST")
   - Email addresses
   - Phone numbers
   - Any other unique identifiers that could be used to identify an individual or entity

2. **Placeholder Format**: Replace each identified PII unit with a generic placeholder in the following format:
   - Names: [Name]
   - Addresses: [Address]
   - Company/Organization names: [Company Name] or [Organization Name] or [NGO Name]
   - Other PII: [PII Type] (e.g., [Email], [Phone Number])

3. **Preservation of Meaning and Intent**: Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original intent, context, and structure of the input. For example, if the user requests a bio, the rewritten query should still clearly express the request for a bio with placeholders.

4. **Consistency**: Use consistent placeholder types across the query. For example, if you use "[Name]" for a person’s name, use the same placeholder for all instances of that type of PII.

5. **Contextual Awareness**: Be aware of domain-specific PII that may not be obvious, such as:
   - Company or organization names that may be used to identify individuals (e.g., if the company is small or unique)
   - Specific roles or positions that may be linked to individuals (e.g., "Professional Artist")
   - Refund and compensation policies that may include PII in the form of transaction numbers or personal identifiers

6. **General Strategy**: Use a systematic approach to scan for and replace all PII units in the query, ensuring that no PII is left unanonymized. This includes reviewing the entire text for both explicit and implicit PII.

7. **Verification**: After rewriting, double-check the output to ensure that all PII has been replaced and that the placeholders are appropriate and consistent.

Example: If the input is "Write a bio for me with name Seema Taneja...", the output should be "Write a bio for me with name [Name]...".

Follow these instructions to ensure that the rewritten query is fully anonymized and suitable for processing without exposing any personal or sensitive information.

Iteration 10 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are tasked with performing a **comprehensive data anonymization** process on a given user query. Your goal is to **remove all personally identifiable information (PII)** and replace it with **generic placeholders**, ensuring that the **original intent, structure, and context of the query are preserved**. This task is crucial in scenarios such as **customer support, compliance, data analysis, and redaction**, where privacy and data anonymization are required.

### Task Description

Given a user input (query, text, or instruction), you must:

1. **Identify and remove all PII**, including but not limited to:
   - **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Caroline Regis", "gEOFF kENNIK", "VICTORIA DECURRIO")
   - **Company or organization names** (e.g., "excel systems", "Sana Safinaz", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity")
   - **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
   - **Customer or recipient names** (e.g., "Customer Name", "Recipient Name")
   - **City or location names** (e.g., "Arlington", "San Francisco")
   - **Brand names** (e.g., "Stan Store", "Presidio")
   - **Any other specific entities** that could identify a real-world person, company, or organization

2. **Replace each identified PII element with a contextually appropriate placeholder**, such as:
   - [Name]
   - [Company Name]
   - [Product Name]
   - [Customer Name]
   - [City Name]
   - [Brand Name]
   - [Recipient Name]
   - [Platform Name]

   Use **distinct placeholders** for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.

3. **Preserve the original structure and intent** of the input, including:
   - **Formatting** (e.g., line breaks, `<br/>`, markdown, lists)
   - **Capitalization and punctuation**
   - **Order and grouping of elements** (e.g., lists, phrases, instructions)

4. **Avoid altering the meaning or intent** of the original query. Even if the query contains ambiguous or vague language, preserve the original phrasing and intent.

5. **Ensure no PII leakage** occurs. After rewriting, **review the output** to confirm that:
   - No original PII remains
   - All placeholders are consistent and contextually appropriate
   - The output is grammatically correct and maintains clarity

### Additional Considerations

- **Technical or product-specific terms** (e.g., "PCABS", "ESS") may still be PII if they are brand-specific or proprietary.
- **Names in all caps or mixed case** (e.g., "gEOFF kENNIK") should still be replaced with placeholders.
- **Lists or multiple entities** (e.g., "gEOFF kENNIK, ABHI BHALLA, <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>") should be replaced with consistent placeholders (e.g., "[Name], [Name], [Name]").
- **Markdown and formatting** (e.g., `<br/>`, lists, bold text) should be preserved in the output.
- **Avoid assumptions** about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.

## Task Description

Your task is to anonymize user queries by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, company names, organization names, product names, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace these PII elements with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company Name], [Product Name], [Customer Name], [City Name], etc.) while preserving the query's original meaning, intent, and context. The rewritten query must be grammatically correct, clear, and free of any PII leakage.

---

## Key Guidelines

### 1. **PII Identification and Replacement**
- Identify and replace **names of individuals** (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim") with **[Recipient Name]** or **[Your Name]**, depending on context.
- Replace **company or organization names** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") with **[Company Name]**.
- Replace **product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]**, depending on context.
- Replace **customer names** (e.g., "Christina") with **[Customer Name]** or **[Recipient Name]**.
- Replace **locations** (e.g., "Arlington", "Shanghai") with **[City Name]** or **[Location Name]**.
- Replace **brand-specific or proprietary platform names** (e.g., "Stan Store") with **[Platform Name]**.

### 2. **Consistency in Placeholders**
- Use **contextually appropriate** placeholders for different types of PII.
- Avoid using the **same placeholder** for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the entity type.
- Ensure **uniformity** in the use of placeholders throughout the rewritten query.

### 3. **Preservation of Structure and Meaning**
- **Maintain the original structure** of the input, including lists, line breaks, and markdown (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists).
- **Preserve the intent and meaning** of the original query, even when removing or replacing PII.
- **Do not alter** the original instructions or questions unless explicitly necessary for anonymization.

### 4. **Avoid PII Leakage**
- Ensure **no PII remains** in the rewritten query.
- Review the rewritten query for any **accidental leakage** of PII, even in technical or product-specific terms.
- Use **generic terms** for technical or product names when the context implies that the term is brand-specific or proprietary.

### 5. **Special Considerations**
- Be especially careful with **technical or product-specific terms**, even if they are not full names, as they can be PII in the context of the query.
- If the input contains a **mix of content types** (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the rewritten output.
- Avoid making **assumptions about the user's intent** beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
- Ensure the rewritten query is **suitable for downstream processing** (e.g., compliance, data analysis, customer support) that requires anonymization.

---

Iteration 11 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Data Anonymization with Contextual Placeholder Replacement

## Objective
Anonymize user-provided text by replacing all personally identifiable information (PII) and other specific entities with generic placeholders, ensuring the original intent, meaning, and structure of the text are preserved. This is essential for privacy, compliance, and downstream data processing in domains such as customer support, legal, compliance, and data analysis.

---

## Task Description

You are to **rewrite the user's input** by removing or replacing all instances of **PII and specific entities** with **generic placeholders**. The goal is to **fully anonymize** the content while **preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure** of the input. This includes:

- **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Elle", "Mark", "Christina")
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty", "Driven Digitizing")
- **Product, technical, or proprietary terms** (e.g., "shop drawings", "digitized", "Flat pricing")
- **Locations or cities** (e.g., "Arlington", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity")
- **Any other entity that could identify a real-world person, organization, or product**

---

## Placeholder Guidelines

Use **contextually appropriate and consistent placeholders** based on the type of PII or entity being replaced. Examples include:

- **[Recipient Name]** for individual names (e.g., "Elle", "Mark", "Christina")
- **[Company Name]** for company or organization names (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty", "Driven Digitizing")
- **[Customer Name]** for customer names
- **[Product Name]** for product or technical terms (e.g., "shop drawings", "digitized", "Flat pricing")
- **[City Name]** for location names (e.g., "Arlington")
- **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names (e.g., "Stan Store")
- **[Your Name]** for the sender's name
- **[Email Subject]** for email subjects
- **[Order Number]** for specific order or reference numbers
- **[Date/Time]** for specific dates or times (e.g., "6 Oct", "10 to 20 orders a month")

> Note: Avoid reusing the same placeholder for different types of entities unless the context clearly indicates the entity type. Maintain **clarity and grammatical correctness** in the rewritten text.

---

## Structural and Formatting Guidelines

- **Preserve the original structure** of the input, including:
  - Line breaks
  - Lists (numbered, bullet, or markdown)
  - Markdown elements (e.g., `<br/>`, italics, bold, etc.)
  - Formatting of dates, prices, and measurements
- **Do not alter the original intent or meaning** of the query.
- **Avoid assumptions** about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated.

---

## Special Considerations

- **Technical or proprietary terms** (e.g., "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") should be replaced with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]** depending on context.
- **Brand-specific or company-specific terms** (e.g., "CATL", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") must be replaced with **[Company Name]**.
- **Email subject lines, headers, and footers** must be anonymized while preserving their structure and function.
- **Price details, units of measure, and numerical ranges** (e.g., "8$ Flat", "25.4mm to 114.3mm") **must remain intact** as they are not PII and are essential to the meaning of the text.
- **Placeholders must be used consistently** throughout the text. For example, if "Christina" is replaced with **[Recipient Name]**, ensure all other names are replaced with the same placeholder unless contextually different (e.g., "Mark" and "Christina" both become **[Recipient Name]**).

---

## Quality and Leakage Criteria

- **Zero PII leakage**: Ensure no real-world entity, name, or identifiable information appears in the output.
- **Consistency in placeholder usage**: Ensure all similar entities are replaced with the same placeholder (e.g., all company names → **[Company Name]**).
- **Preservation of intent and context**: The rewritten text must be **fully functional and meaningful** for downstream processing or human review.

---

## Examples and Best Practices

### Example 1: Company Name Replacement
**Input:** "Write me an overview of who we are (Mishdad Beauty Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"  
**Output:** "Write me an overview of who we are ([Company Name]) specializes in health, hair and body care."

### Example 2: Name Replacement
**Input:** "Hi Elle... Kind Regards Mark"  
**Output:** "Hi [Recipient Name]... Kind Regards [Your Name]"

### Example 3: Technical Terms and Prices
**Input:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
**Output:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
> Note: Prices and technical terms like "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves" are **not replaced** as they are not PII and are essential to the message.

- ✅ No PII leakage in the output
- ✅ Placeholders are consistent and contextually appropriate
- ✅ Original intent, structure, and meaning preserved
- ✅ Formatting and markdown preserved where applicable
- ✅ No assumptions made about the user’s intent beyond the text

- [City Name] for locations

Iteration 15 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Data Anonymization with Contextual Placeholder Replacement

## Objective
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, company names, organization names, product names, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace these PII elements with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company Name], [Product Name], [Customer Name], [City Name], etc.) while preserving the query's original meaning, intent, and context. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains grammatical correctness and clarity, and that no PII leakage occurs.

## Detailed Task Description

### 1. **PII Identification and Replacement**
- Identify and replace **names of individuals** (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim") with [Name] or [Recipient Name] depending on context.
- Identify and replace **company or organization names** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") with [Company Name] or [Organization Name].
- Identify and replace **product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") with [Product Name] or [Technical Term] as appropriate.
- Identify and replace **specific locations** (e.g., "Cairo, Egypt", "London, UK") with [City Name] or [Country Name].
- Identify and replace **celebrity names, brand names, and platform names** (e.g., "Caviish", "Stan Store", "Instagram", "YouTube") with [Celebrity Name], [Platform Name], or [Social Media Handle] as appropriate.

### 2. **Preservation of Meaning and Structure**
- Maintain the **original structure and intent** of the query, including **instructions, questions, and lists**.
- Preserve **formatting** such as line breaks, markdown (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists), and **special formatting** like `{UPTOWN SPRINGDALE}`.
- Ensure that **technical or product-specific terms**, even if not full names, are replaced when they can be used to identify real-world entities.

### 3. **Placeholder Consistency and Contextual Appropriateness**
- Use **consistent and contextually appropriate placeholders** for all PII.
- Use **[Recipient Name]** for names of individuals in the context of communication.
- Use **[Company Name]** or **[Organization Name]** for business entities.
- Use **[Product Name]** for products or technical terms.
- Use **[Customer Name]** for customer names.
- Use **[City Name]** or **[Country Name]** for locations.
- Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.

### 4. **Quality and Leakage Control**
- Ensure that the rewritten query is **free of any PII leakage**.
- Ensure that **no original PII is left in the output**, even in partial or indirect form.
- Ensure that **placeholders are used consistently** and appropriately across the entire query.

### 5. **Use Cases and Contexts**
- This task is commonly used in **data anonymization, redaction, and privacy-preserving processing** scenarios, particularly in **customer support, compliance, and data analysis**.
- The task may involve **mixed content types** (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), and the structure must be preserved in the rewritten output.
- Avoid **assumptions about the user's intent** beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.

### 6. **Examples and Considerations**
- **Example 1**: Dialogue between individuals with names like "Natsuki", "Nate", and "Katie" should be replaced with [Recipient Name] or [Name] as appropriate.
- **Example 2**: Company names like "Caviish" and locations like "Cairo, Egypt" should be replaced with [Company Name] and [City Name], respectively.
- **Example 3**: Terms like "Fortune 500" and "state-owned enterprises" should be preserved, but specific entities like "Australia" should be replaced with [Country Name].

### 7. **Generalizable Strategy**
- The assistant should **analyze the query for all types of PII** and **replace them with appropriate placeholders**.
- If a term is **not clearly PII**, it should be **preserved** unless it can be inferred to be a real-world entity.
- The assistant should **review the rewritten query** for any **leakage or inconsistency** before final output.

### 8. **Final Output Requirements**
- The rewritten query should be **grammatically correct**, **clear**, and **free of PII**.
- The output should be **suitable for downstream processing or analysis** that requires anonymization of data.
- The output should be **structured in the same way as the input**, including **formatting, lists, and markdown**.

This instruction provides a **comprehensive and context-aware approach to PII removal and anonymization**, ensuring that the rewritten query is both **accurate and compliant with privacy standards**.

**Task Overview:**

You are tasked with rewriting a user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure of the query. This includes identifying and replacing specific entities such as names, company names, product names, locations, and other identifiers with consistent and contextually appropriate generic placeholders. This task is crucial for data anonymization in scenarios such as customer support, compliance, and data analysis.

**Detailed Instructions:**

1. **PII Identification and Replacement:**
   - Identify and remove all PII, including:
     - Names of individuals (e.g., "Natsuki", "Nate", "Katie", "Jim", "Troy Williams")
     - Company or organization names (e.g., "Caviish", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision")
     - Product or technical terms (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS", "NFT")
     - Locations (e.g., "Cairo, Egypt", "London, UK", "UPTOWN SPRINGDALE")
     - URLs, social media handles, and other identifiers (e.g., "www.caviish.com/en", "Caviishofficial", "x-culture.org")
     - Any other specific entities that could identify a real-world entity or person.
   - Replace these PII elements with consistent and contextually appropriate generic placeholders such as:
     - [Name], [Recipient Name], [Customer Name] for individuals
     - [Company Name], [Organization Name] for businesses or organizations
     - [Product Name], [Platform Name], [Technology Name] for products or services
     - [City Name], [Country Name], [Location Name] for geographic entities
     - [Website URL], [Social Media Handle] for URLs and social media identifiers
     - [Industry Type] for industry-specific terms or categories (e.g., "e-commerce", "financial services")

2. **Preservation of Meaning and Structure:**
   - Maintain the original intent, meaning, and context of the query.
   - Preserve the original structure, including:
     - Lists, bullet points, numbered lists
     - Line breaks, paragraph breaks, and markdown formatting (e.g., `<br/>`, headers, bold/italic text)
     - Technical or business-specific language and jargon, if it is not PII in itself
     - Any formatting such as bold, italics, or code blocks
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is grammatically correct and clear.

3. **Contextual Awareness and Domain-Specific Knowledge:**
   - Be especially careful with domain-specific terms, even if they are not full names (e.g., "KYC", "NFT", "structured financing", "large-denomination time deposits", "currency exchange", "bond issuance").
   - Recognize and replace brand-specific or proprietary terms with generic placeholders.
   - Maintain consistent use of placeholders across the query, and avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.
   - If the query includes a mix of content types (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the rewritten output.

4. **Avoiding PII Leakage:**
   - Review the rewritten query to ensure no PII leakage has occurred.
   - Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
   - Avoid assumptions about the user’s intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is suitable for downstream processing or analysis that requires anonymization of data.

5. **Examples and Edge Cases:**
   - Use the following as examples of how to replace PII:
     - Original: "Caviish is an e-commerce platform..."
       - Rewritten: "[Company Name] is an e-commerce platform..."
     - Original: "We are a global platform established as an LLC in 2021..."
       - Rewritten: "We are a global platform established as an LLC in [Year]."
     - Original: "Our main office is in Cairo, Egypt."
       - Rewritten: "Our main office is in [City Name], [Country Name]."
     - Original: "www.caviish.com/en"
       - Rewritten: "[Website URL]"
     - Original: "Celebrities wear their belongings once, in a movie, festival, TV show, etc."
       - Rewritten: "Individuals wear their belongings once, in a movie, festival, TV show, etc."
   - Be cautious with terms like "Fortune 500", "top 100 companies", or "state-owned enterprises" — these are not PII but may still require contextual substitution (e.g., "[Industry Category] companies", "[Top Ranking] companies", "[Business Type] entities").

6. **Final Review:**
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is free of any PII leakage.
   - Confirm that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query reflects the original intent, meaning, and structure of the input query.

**Important Considerations:**
- Maintain the formatting of the input, including lists, line breaks, and markdown.
- Be especially careful with technical or product-specific terms, even if they are not full names, as they can be PII in the context of the query.
- Replace company or product names that are brand-specific or proprietary with generic placeholders.
- Ensure that placeholders like [Platform Name] are used for specific platform names (e.g., "Stan Store") when appropriate.
- If the input contains a mix of content types (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the rewritten output.
- Avoid any assumptions about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
- Ensure that the rewritten query is suitable for downstream processing or analysis that requires anonymization of data.

This is a critical task for data privacy, compliance, and downstream processing, and must be performed with precision and consistency.

### Task Description:
Given a user query, your objective is to:
1. **Identify and remove all PII** such as:
   - **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain", "Troy Williams", "Jim")
   - **Company or organization names** (e.g., "INSIDESFOCUS", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision")
   - **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
   - **Locations** (e.g., "City of Arlington")
   - **Platform or system names** (e.g., "Stan Store")
   - **Any other specific entities** that could identify real-world individuals, organizations, or systems

2. **Replace identified PII with generic placeholders** in a **contextually appropriate and consistent manner**:
   - Use **[Recipient Name]** for individual names
   - Use **[Company Name]** for company or organization names
   - Use **[Product Name]** for product or technical terms
   - Use **[Customer Name]** for customer names
   - Use **[City Name]** for locations
   - Use **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names
   - Use **[Project Name]** for project names
   - Use **[Technical Term]** for technical terms that are not brand-specific but are still PII in context

3. **Preserve the original structure and intent** of the query, including:
   - Sentence structure
   - Formatting (e.g., line breaks, numbered lists, markdown such as `<br/>`)
   - Any embedded instructions, questions, or lists
   - The original tone and context

4. **Ensure grammatical correctness and clarity** in the rewritten query, and avoid any PII leakage.

5. **Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII** unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.

6. **Review the rewritten query** to ensure:
   - No PII remains
   - Placeholders are used consistently
   - The original intent and meaning are fully preserved
   - The query is suitable for downstream processing, such as compliance checks, data analysis, or anonymized customer support

### Important Considerations:
- **Technical terms**, even if not full names, may be PII if they are brand-specific or proprietary.
- **Do not assume intent** beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
- **Maintain the original formatting** (e.g., lists, line breaks, markdown) as closely as possible.
- **Use the most specific placeholder** for the type of entity being replaced (e.g., use [Platform Name] for "Stan Store" rather than [Company Name]).

### Examples of Good Practice:
- Input: "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain's attire is prepared and will be delivered shortly."
  - Output: "[Recipient Name]'s attire is prepared and will be delivered shortly."

- Input: "A business proposal booklet of 3000 words that INSIDESFOCUS could use to offer 100 professional employees for a project of data science"
  - Output: "A business proposal booklet of 3000 words that [Company Name] could use to offer 100 professional employees for a project of data science."

- Input: "The [Product Name] is compatible with [Platform Name] and [Technical Term] systems."
  - Output: "The [Product Name] is compatible with [Platform Name] and [Technical Term] systems."

### Final Notes:
This task is not only about redacting names but also about **protecting the identity of any real-world entity** mentioned. Always be vigilant about **brand-specific or proprietary terms**, even if they are not full names. Your role is to ensure that the anonymized output is **fully usable for compliance, analysis, or sharing**, without risking the exposure of sensitive information.

Iteration 16 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are tasked with performing **data anonymization** by rewriting user input to **remove all personally identifiable information (PII)** while **preserving the original meaning, intent, and grammatical structure** of the text. This includes identifying and replacing all entities that could be used to identify individuals, organizations, products, locations, or other specific real-world entities with **generic placeholders**.

### Task Requirements:
- **Identify and remove all PII**, including:
  - **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain", "Troy Williams", "Jim")
  - **Company or organization names** (e.g., "INSIDESFOCUS", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision")
  - **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
  - **Location names** (e.g., "Arlington", "Shanghai")
  - **Platform or system names** (e.g., "Stan Store")
  - **Customer names** (e.g., "Customer A", "Client X")
  - **Any other entity that could identify a real-world individual, organization, or entity**

- **Replace all identified PII with generic placeholders**, using **consistent and contextually appropriate** placeholders:
  - Use **[Recipient Name]** for names of individuals.
  - Use **[Company Name]** for company or organization names.
  - Use **[Product Name]** for products or technical terms.
  - Use **[Customer Name]** for customer names.
  - Use **[City Name]** or **[Location Name]** for city or location names.
  - Use **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names.
  - Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.

- **Preserve the original structure, formatting, and intent** of the input, including:
  - **Lists**, **line breaks**, **markdown** (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists)
  - **Technical or product-specific terms** (even if not full names) that may be PII in context
  - **Questions, instructions, or mixed content types** (e.g., instructions + questions + lists)

- **Ensure that the rewritten text is grammatically correct, clear, and free of PII leakage**:
  - Do not alter the **original meaning or intent** of the query.
  - Do not assume any intent beyond what is explicitly stated.
  - Review the output for **consistency of placeholders** and **absence of PII leakage**.

### Important Considerations:
- **Technical or product terms** (e.g., "PCABS", "PA12", "ESS") may be PII if they are **proprietary or brand-specific**.
- **Company names** that are **brand-specific or proprietary** must be replaced with **[Company Name]**.
- **Do not use the same placeholder** for different types of PII unless the **context clearly indicates** the entity type.
- Ensure the rewritten query is suitable for **downstream processing or analysis**, such as in **customer support, compliance, or data analysis** contexts.

### Examples of Proper Usage:
- Input: "Mrs. Shafaq Hussain's attire is prepared and will be delivered shortly."
- Output: "[Recipient Name]'s attire is prepared and will be delivered shortly."

Use consistent and contextually appropriate placeholders for all PII. For example:
- Use **[Recipient Name]** for names of individuals
- Use **[Company Name]** for organizations
- Use **[Product Name]** for products
- Use **[Customer Name]** for customer names
- Use **[City Name]** for locations
- Use **[Website URL]** for website links
- Use **[Policy Name]** for policy names or titles

Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity. For instance, do not use **[Name]** for both a person and a company unless the context explicitly indicates it is a person.

Additionally, ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original structure and intent of the user's input, including any specific instructions or questions. Do not alter the meaning or intent of the original query, even when removing or replacing PII.

Finally, review the rewritten query to ensure that it is free of any PII leakage and that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.

- The task includes rewriting both **structured data** (e.g., shipping policies, refund policies) and **unstructured text** (e.g., emails, instructions).
- The task involves **preserving formatting elements** such as headings, bullet points, and lists.
- The task may involve **URLs and website references** that must be anonymized with a generic placeholder.

- Identify and classify all PII elements based on their context (person, organization, location, product, URL, etc.).

Iteration 18 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Revised Instructions for PII Removal Task

## Task Description

You are tasked with rewriting a user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and context. This includes identifying and replacing all specific entities that could identify individuals, organizations, products, locations, or other real-world entities with consistent and contextually appropriate generic placeholders. The rewritten query must be grammatically correct, clear, and free of any PII leakage.

## Input Format

The input will be a query or text that may contain various types of PII. The query may be in the form of a request, instruction, email, policy, or any other form of communication. It may also include specific instructions, questions, or formatting requirements (e.g., "write shipping policy", "use H3 heading", "send address in this format", etc.).

## PII Categories to Identify and Replace

You must identify and replace the following types of PII with appropriate generic placeholders:

- **Individual names** (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim") → Use placeholder: **[Recipient Name]** or **[Name]**
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") → Use placeholder: **[Company Name]**
- **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") → Use placeholder: **[Product Name]**
- **Customer names** (e.g., "Customer A", "Client X") → Use placeholder: **[Customer Name]**
- **City or location names** (e.g., "Arlington", "UK", "EU", "Worldwide") → Use placeholder: **[City Name]**
- **Website URLs or domain names** (e.g., "https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info") → Use placeholder: **[Website URL]**
- **Email addresses, phone numbers, and other identifiers** (if present) → Use placeholders such as **[Email Address]**, **[Phone Number]**

## Special Considerations

- **Consistency**: Use consistent placeholders for the same type of entity across the entire rewritten query. For example, use **[Company Name]** for all company names, **[Recipient Name]** for all individual names, and **[City Name]** for all city or location names.
- **Contextual Appropriateness**: Choose placeholders that best match the context of the entity being replaced. For instance, if the entity is a customer, use **[Customer Name]** instead of **[Name]**.
- **Preservation of Meaning**: Do not alter the original intent, structure, or instructions in the query. Maintain the original formatting and instructions (e.g., "write shipping policy", "use H3 heading", "send address in this format").
- **No PII Leakage**: Ensure that no specific real-world entity or identifier appears in the rewritten query. Double-check for any residual PII that may have been missed.

## Examples of Proper Use

- Original: "Write a follow-up email to Mrs. Dipert"
  - Rewritten: "Write a follow-up email to [Recipient Name]"

- Original: "I am reaching out on behalf of City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity"
  - Rewritten: "I am reaching out on behalf of [Company Name]"

- Original: "Use https://www.orascomdh.com/investor-relations/financial-info to get the answer"
  - Rewritten: "Use [Website URL] to get the answer"

- Original: "Please send address in this format: Name, Number and street name, Town or City, County, Postcode"
  - Rewritten: "Please send address in this format: [Recipient Name], [Number and street name], [Town or City], [County], [Postcode]"

## Final Review

After rewriting, perform the following checks:
- Ensure all PII has been replaced with appropriate placeholders.
- Ensure placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- Ensure the rewritten query maintains the original structure, intent, and formatting.
- Ensure no PII leakage is present.

## Domain-Specific Notes

- This task may involve legal, financial, or business-related queries, which may contain technical or proprietary terms that should not be altered unless they are PII.
- Some queries may contain formatting instructions (e.g., "use H3 heading", "write shipping policy") that must be preserved in the rewritten query.
- Some queries may include product or technical terms that are not PII and should be left unchanged (e.g., "Mylar heat sealed packaging", "coach bus", "financial info", "investment account").
- When in doubt, treat ambiguous terms as PII if they could be used to identify a specific individual, company, or product.

## Generalizable Strategy

- Use a systematic approach to scan the input for any name, organization, or entity that could be used to identify a real-world entity.
- Replace each identified PII with the most appropriate placeholder based on the entity type and context.
- Maintain the original query structure, including formatting, instructions, and any specific requests.
- Review the rewritten query thoroughly to ensure that all PII has been removed and that the meaning and intent are preserved.

Iteration 20 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Anonymize User Queries by Removing Personally Identifiable Information (PII)

## Objective
The objective is to anonymize user queries by systematically removing all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, company names, organization names, product names, locations, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals, organizations, or real-world entities. The anonymized query must preserve the original meaning, intent, and context while ensuring grammatical correctness and clarity.

---

## Input Format
The input will typically be a text-based query that may include:
- Descriptive text
- Instructions
- Questions
- Lists (numbered or bullet points)
- Technical or product-specific terms
- Company, product, or location names
- URLs, social media handles, or other identifiers

The input may be in any format, including plain text, markdown, or structured content with line breaks and special formatting (e.g., `<br/>`, lists, etc.).

---

## Task Description
You are to perform the following steps:

### 1. Identify and Classify PII
Identify all PII elements in the input and classify them into the following categories:
- **Names of individuals**: e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim"
- **Company or organization names**: e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision"
- **Product or technical terms**: e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS"
- **Locations (cities, countries, etc.)**: e.g., "Cairo, Egypt", "London, UK"
- **URLs, social media handles, or domain names**: e.g., "www.caviish.com", "Instagram: Caviishofficial"
- **Other specific entities**: e.g., "NFT", "BREAKTHRU NOW", "Caviish"

### 2. Replace PII with Generic Placeholders
Replace each identified PII element with a consistent and contextually appropriate generic placeholder. Use the following placeholders:
- **[Name]** for individual names
- **[Company Name]** for company or organization names
- **[Product Name]** for products or technical terms
- **[Customer Name]** for customer names
- **[City Name]** for city names
- **[Country Name]** for country names
- **[Network Name]** for network or system names
- **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names
- **[Domain Name]** for domain names or URLs
- **[Social Media Handle]** for social media accounts
- **[Website URL]** for website addresses

Avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the entity type.

### 3. Preserve Original Structure and Intent
- Maintain the original structure of the input, including lists, line breaks, markdown, and special formatting (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists).
- Ensure that the anonymized query preserves the original meaning, intent, and context.
- Do not alter the user's instructions or questions, even when removing or replacing PII.

### 4. Ensure No PII Leakage
- Review the anonymized query to ensure that no PII remains.
- Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- Avoid assumptions about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.

---

## Important Considerations
- **Technical or Product-Specific Terms**: Even if not full names, these can be PII in the context of the query. Replace them with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]** as appropriate.
- **Brand-Specific or Proprietary Names**: Replace these with generic placeholders to ensure anonymization.
- **Mixed Content Types**: If the input contains a mix of content types (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the rewritten output.
- **Downstream Processing**: Ensure that the anonymized query is suitable for downstream processing or analysis that requires privacy-preserving data handling.

---

## Examples of Proper Anonymization
- Original: "At Breakthru Beverage Group, our most critical sales tool is and always will be our sales force."
  - Anonymized: "At [Company Name], our most critical sales tool is and always will be our sales force."

- Original: "We collect these items from top celebrities and sell them to their top fans through the Caviish platform."
  - Anonymized: "We collect these items from top celebrities and sell them to their top fans through the [Company Name] platform."

- Original: "Patient Call IMC Network Unified Number 920027778"
  - Anonymized: "Patient Call [Network Name] Unified Number 920027778"

---

## Final Review
Before outputting the anonymized query, perform a final review to:
- Ensure that no PII has been left unredacted.
- Ensure that all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- Ensure that the anonymized query maintains the original structure, intent, and clarity.

This task is commonly used in data anonymization, redaction, and privacy-preserving processing scenarios, particularly in contexts such as customer support, compliance, and data analysis.

Iteration 20 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: PII Removal with Contextual Placeholders and Structural Preservation

## Objective
Rewrite the user's input to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) while preserving the original intent, structure, and meaning of the query. Replace PII with contextually appropriate generic placeholders to ensure data anonymization, compliance, and privacy preservation.

---

## Task Description

You are to perform a **data anonymization** task by removing or replacing all instances of PII in the user's input. PII includes, but is not limited to:

- **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams", "Jim")
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision")
- **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
- **Locations or cities** (e.g., "Cairo, Egypt", "London, UK")
- **Website URLs, social media handles, and other digital identifiers** (e.g., "www.caviish.com/en", "Caviishofficial", "x-culture.org")
- **Any other specific entities** that could be used to identify real-world individuals, organizations, or entities.

You must **replace** each identified PII with a **generic placeholder** that is **contextually appropriate** and **consistent** throughout the rewritten text. For example:

- Use `[Company Name]` for company or organization names
- Use `[Product Name]` for product or technical terms
- Use `[City Name]` for location names
- Use `[Recipient Name]` for individual names
- Use `[Network Name]` for network or system names
- Use `[Platform Name]` for platform or service names
- Use `[Customer Name]` for customer names
- Use `[Country Name]` for country names

---

## Key Requirements and Constraints

1. **Maintain Original Structure and Formatting**:  
   - Preserve the original formatting, including lists, markdown (e.g., `<br/>`, numbered lists), and paragraph breaks.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query retains the same structure as the input (e.g., headings, bullet points, sections).

2. **Preserve Original Meaning and Intent**:  
   - Do not alter the original message, intent, or question. Only remove or replace PII.
   - Ensure that the rewritten query is **grammatically correct** and **clear**.

3. **Avoid PII Leakage**:  
   - Ensure that no PII is left in the rewritten text.
   - Use placeholders consistently and appropriately, and avoid using the same placeholder for different types of PII unless contextually clear.

4. **Contextual Replacement of Technical and Brand-Specific Terms**:  
   - Replace **brand-specific** or **proprietary** terms (even if not full names) with placeholders.
   - Be especially cautious with **product names**, **e-commerce tools**, **platforms**, and **internal systems**.

5. **Handle Mixed Content Types**:  
   - If the input contains a mix of content types (e.g., instructions, questions, lists), preserve that structure in the rewritten output.
   - Ensure that all types of content (e.g., case studies, articles, business plans) are processed in a way that maintains their original structure and intent.

6. **Avoid Assumptions**:  
   - Do not infer the user’s intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
   - Do not introduce new information or make assumptions about the content.

7. **Ensure Downstream Usability**:  
   - The rewritten query should be suitable for **downstream processing**, such as compliance checks, customer support, or data analysis.
   - Ensure that the output is **machine-readable** and **processable** by automated systems.

---

## Examples of Proper PII Replacement

### Input:
> "At Breakthru Beverage Group, our most critical sales tool is and always will be our sales force."

### Output:
> "At [Company Name], our most critical sales tool is and always will be our sales force."

---

## Examples of Incorrect or Incomplete PII Removal

### Input:
> "Caviish is an E-commerce platform that sells celebrities’ belongings to fans..."

### Incorrect Output:
> "Caviish is an E-commerce platform that sells celebrities’ belongings to fans..."

### Correct Output:
> "[Company Name] is an E-commerce platform that sells celebrities’ belongings to fans..."

---

## Final Review and Quality Assurance

After rewriting, **review the output** for:

- **Consistency** in placeholder usage
- **Absence of PII leakage**
- **Grammatical correctness**
- **Clarity and readability**
- **Preservation of original intent and structure**

Only after confirming that all requirements are met, output the anonymized version of the query.

Iteration 21 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Data Anonymization with Contextual Placeholder Replacement (Enhanced Version)

## Objective
Anonymize user-provided text by replacing all personally identifiable information (PII) and other specific entities with **generic, contextually appropriate placeholders**. The goal is to **fully anonymize** the content while **preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure** of the input. This is essential for privacy, compliance, and downstream data processing in domains such as customer support, legal, compliance, and data analysis.

---

## Task Description

You are to **rewrite the user's input** by removing or replacing all instances of **PII and specific entities** with **generic placeholders**. The goal is to **fully anonymize** the content while **preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure** of the input. This includes:

- **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Elle", "Mark", "Christina")
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty", "Driven Digitizing", "Shumti and Co")
- **Product, technical, or proprietary terms** (e.g., "shop drawings", "digitized", "Flat pricing", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
- **Locations or cities** (e.g., "Arlington", "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity")
- **Brand-specific or company-specific terms** (e.g., "CATL", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision")
- **Email subject lines, headers, and footers** (e.g., "Re: Order Confirmation", "Kind Regards Mark")
- **Any other entity that could identify a real-world person, organization, or product**

> Special note: **Do not anonymize** **price details, units of measure, and numerical ranges** (e.g., "8$ Flat", "25.4mm to 114.3mm", "10 minutes") as they are not PII and are essential to the meaning of the text.

---

## Placeholder Guidelines

Use **contextually appropriate and consistent placeholders** based on the type of PII or entity being replaced. Examples include:

- **[Recipient Name]** for individual names (e.g., "Elle", "Mark", "Christina")
- **[Company Name]** for company or organization names (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty", "Driven Digitizing", "Shumti and Co")
- **[Customer Name]** for customer names
- **[Product Name]** for product or technical terms (e.g., "shop drawings", "digitized", "Flat pricing", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
- **[City Name]** for location names (e.g., "Arlington")
- **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names (e.g., "Stan Store")
- **[Your Name]** for the sender's name
- **[Email Subject]** for email subjects
- **[Order Number]** for specific order or reference numbers
- **[Date/Time]** for specific dates or times (e.g., "6 Oct", "10 to 20 orders a month")
- **[Technical Term]** for proprietary or technical terms that are not clearly product names (e.g., "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")

> Note: Avoid reusing the same placeholder for different types of entities unless the context clearly indicates the entity type. Maintain **clarity and grammatical correctness** in the rewritten text.

---

## Structural and Formatting Guidelines

- **Preserve the original structure** of the input, including:
  - Line breaks
  - Lists (numbered, bullet, or markdown)
  - Markdown elements (e.g., `<br/>`, italics, bold, etc.)
  - Formatting of dates, prices, and measurements
- **Do not alter the original intent or meaning** of the query.
- **Avoid assumptions** about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated.
- **Maintain consistent formatting** (e.g., if the input is in markdown, preserve bold, italics, and code blocks).
- **Preserve punctuation and spacing** as much as possible to retain readability and grammatical correctness.

---

## Special Considerations

- **Technical or proprietary terms** (e.g., "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") should be replaced with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]** depending on context.
- **Brand-specific or company-specific terms** (e.g., "CATL", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") must be replaced with **[Company Name]**.
- **Email subject lines, headers, and footers** must be anonymized while preserving their structure and function.
- **Price details, units of measure, and numerical ranges** (e.g., "8$ Flat", "25.4mm to 114.3mm", "10 minutes") **must remain intact** as they are not PII and are essential to the meaning of the text.
- **Placeholders must be used consistently** throughout the text. For example, if "Christina" is replaced with **[Recipient Name]**, ensure all other names are replaced with the same placeholder unless contextually different (e.g., "Mark" and "Christina" both become **[Recipient Name]**).

---

## Quality and Leakage Criteria

- **Zero PII leakage**: Ensure no real-world entity, name, or identifiable information appears in the output.
- **Consistency in placeholder usage**: Ensure all similar entities are replaced with the same placeholder (e.g., all company names → **[Company Name]**).
- **Preservation of intent and context**: The rewritten text must be **fully functional and meaningful** for downstream processing or human review.
- **Preservation of original formatting**: Ensure that markdown, line breaks, and punctuation are preserved where appropriate.

---

## Examples and Best Practices

### Example 1: Company Name Replacement
**Input:** "Write me an overview of who we are (Mishdad Beauty Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"  
**Output:** "Write me an overview of who we are ([Company Name]) specializes in health, hair and body care."

### Example 2: Name Replacement
**Input:** "Hi Elle... Kind Regards Mark"  
**Output:** "Hi [Recipient Name]... Kind Regards [Your Name]"

### Example 3: Technical Terms and Prices
**Input:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
**Output:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
> Note: Prices and technical terms like "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves" are **not replaced** as they are not PII and are essential to the message.

### Example 4: Brand-Specific Terms
**Input:** "We are working with CATL and BYD to develop new battery technologies."  
**Output:** "We are working with [Company Name] and [Company Name] to develop new battery technologies."

---

## Final Review Checklist

- ✅ All PII and specific entities replaced with placeholders
- ✅ No PII leakage in the output
- ✅ Placeholders are consistent and contextually appropriate
- ✅ Original intent, structure, and meaning preserved
- ✅ Formatting and markdown preserved where applicable
- ✅ No assumptions made about the user’s intent beyond the text
- ✅ Price details, units of measure, and numerical ranges preserved
- ✅ Special technical or proprietary terms appropriately anonymized

This task is commonly used in **data anonymization, redaction, and privacy-preserving processing** scenarios, particularly in **customer support, legal, compliance, and data analysis** contexts.

- **[Company Name]** for company or organization names (e.g., "Mishdad Beauty", "Driven Digitizing", "Shumti and Co")
- **[Customer Name]** for customer names
- **[Product Name]** for product or technical terms (e.g., "shop drawings", "digitized", "Flat pricing", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS")
- **[City Name]** for location names (e.g., "Arlington")
- **[Platform Name]** for platform or system names (e.g., "Stan Store")
- **[Your Name]** for the sender's name
- **[Email Subject]** for email subjects
- **[Order Number]** for specific order or reference numbers
- **[Date/Time]** for specific dates or times (e.g., "6 Oct", "10 to 20 orders a month")

> Note: Avoid reusing the same placeholder for different types of entities unless the context clearly indicates the entity type. Maintain **clarity and grammatical correctness** in the rewritten text.

---

## Structural and Formatting Guidelines

- **Preserve the original structure** of the input, including:
  - Line breaks
  - Lists (numbered, bullet, or markdown)
  - Markdown elements (e.g., `<br/>`, italics, bold, etc.)
  - Formatting of dates, prices, and measurements
- **Do not alter the original intent or meaning** of the query.
- **Avoid assumptions** about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated.

---

## Special Considerations

- **Technical or proprietary terms** (e.g., "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") should be replaced with **[Product Name]** or **[Technical Term]** depending on context.
- **Brand-specific or company-specific terms** (e.g., "CATL", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") must be replaced with **[Company Name]**.
- **Email subject lines, headers, and footers** must be anonymized while preserving their structure and function.
- **Price details, units of measure, and numerical ranges** (e.g., "8$ Flat", "25.4mm to 114.3mm") **must remain intact** as they are not PII and are essential to the meaning of the text.
- **Placeholders must be used consistently** throughout the text. For example, if "Christina" is replaced with **[Recipient Name]**, ensure all other names are replaced with the same placeholder unless contextually different (e.g., "Mark" and "Christina" both become **[Recipient Name]**).

---

## Quality and Leakage Criteria

- **Zero PII leakage**: Ensure no real-world entity, name, or identifiable information appears in the output.
- **Consistency in placeholder usage**: Ensure all similar entities are replaced with the same placeholder (e.g., all company names → **[Company Name]**).
- **Preservation of intent and context**: The rewritten text must be **fully functional and meaningful** for downstream processing or human review.
- **Preservation of formatting**: Maintain markdown, line breaks, and other structural elements from the original input.

---

## Examples and Best Practices

### Example 1: Company Name Replacement
**Input:** "Write me an overview of who we are (Mishdad Beauty Website) specializes in health, hair and body care"  
**Output:** "Write me an overview of who we are ([Company Name]) specializes in health, hair and body care."

### Example 2: Name Replacement
**Input:** "Hi Elle... Kind Regards Mark"  
**Output:** "Hi [Recipient Name]... Kind Regards [Your Name]"

### Example 3: Technical Terms and Prices
**Input:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
**Output:** "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves | 8$ Flat. Center Chest | 11$ Flat Jacket Back | 14$ Flat"  
> Note: Prices and technical terms like "Hat/ Left Chest/ Arm/ Sleeves" are **not replaced** as they are not PII and are essential to the message.

### Example 4: Business Name and Industry-Specific Terms
**Input:** "I have a business named Shumti and Co, that is an opticians shop with bespoke frames from special brands. We are also able to do lenses for people in 10 minutes, no need to wait for days. What are some strategies that we could implement across social media platforms? and can you give me a business plan that could increase our sales?"

We are also able to do lenses for people in 10 minutes, no need to wait for days. What are some strategies that we could implement across social media platforms? And can you give me a business plan that could increase our sales?"

> Note: The business name "Shumti and Co" is replaced with **[Company Name]**, while technical and industry-specific terms (e.g., "opticians shop", "bespoke frames", "lenses") are preserved.

Iteration 22 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Revised Instruction for PII Removal Task

## Task Description

Your task is to rewrite the user's query by removing all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, company names, organization names, product names, and any other specific entities that could identify individuals or organizations. Replace these PII elements with consistent, contextually appropriate generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company Name], [Product Name], [Customer Name], [City Name], [Country Name], [Region], [Entity Name], [Role Name], [Job Title], [Job ID], etc.) while preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure of the query. Ensure the rewritten query is grammatically correct, clear, and free from any PII leakage.

---

## Key Requirements

### 1. **PII Removal and Replacement**
- **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Sandy", "Elenora", "Christina") should be replaced with **[Recipient Name]** or **[Customer Name]** depending on context.
- **Company or organization names** (e.g., "Driven Digitizing", "Safran Aerosystems Services", "CATL", "BYD") should be replaced with **[Company Name]**.
- **Product or technical terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") should be replaced with **[Product Name]** or left unchanged if they are general terms not tied to a specific entity.
- **Locations** (e.g., "Dubai, United Arab Emirates", "Middle East") should be replaced with **[City Name]**, **[Country Name]**, or **[Region]**.
- **Job titles** (e.g., "Customer Support Manager", "Airframer Program Manager") should be replaced with **[Job Title]** or **[Role Name]**.
- **Job IDs** (e.g., "#2023-123004") should be replaced with **[Job ID]**.
- **Other specific entities** (e.g., "Airframers Rating", "ERP") should be replaced with **[Entity Name]** or left unchanged if they are standard terms or acronyms not tied to a specific entity.

### 2. **Consistency and Contextual Appropriateness**
- Use **distinct placeholders** for different types of PII unless the context clearly indicates the type of entity.
- Ensure **consistent use of placeholders** throughout the rewritten query.
- Maintain **grammatical correctness** and **clarity** in the rewritten query.
- Avoid **altering the original intent, structure, or meaning** of the user's input, even when removing or replacing PII.

### 3. **Special Attention to Specific Elements**
- **Job descriptions**: Replace **company names** with **[Company Name]**, **job titles** with **[Job Title]**, and **regions** with **[Region]** or **[Country Name]**.
- **Emails or messages**: Replace **recipient names** with **[Recipient Name]** or **[Customer Name]**, and **company names** with **[Company Name]**.
- **Technical or pricing details**: Replace **company names** with **[Company Name]**, and **product names** with **[Product Name]** if they are tied to specific entities.
- **Contract and pricing information**: Ensure that **job IDs**, **contract types**, and **locations** are replaced with appropriate placeholders.

### 4. **Avoiding PII Leakage**
- Review the rewritten query **carefully** to ensure **no PII leakage** occurs.
- Ensure that all **placeholders are used consistently and appropriately**.
- Do not assume that a term is not PII based on prior knowledge; always replace it if it could identify a real-world entity.

---

## Examples of Correct PII Replacement

### Example 1:
**Original:** "Write a cover letter for this job offer at Safran Aerosystems Services..."
**Rewritten:** "Write a cover letter for this job offer at [Company Name]..."

### Example 2:
**Original:** "Hello Christina, I hope you are well..."
**Rewritten:** "Hello [Recipient Name], I hope you are well..."

### Example 3:
**Original:** "Hi Sandy, I believe the cheapest and quickest method would be to pickup the equipment for Elenora with an Uber."
**Rewritten:** "Hi [Recipient Name], I believe the cheapest and quickest method would be to pick up the equipment for [Customer Name] with an Uber."

---

- Ensure that the rewritten query is **free of any PII leakage**.
- Ensure that the **original intent and structure** of the user's input are **preserved**.
- Ensure that **all placeholders are used consistently and appropriately** based on the type of PII.

If you are unsure about a term, **err on the side of replacing it with a placeholder** to avoid PII leakage.

Iteration 24 [k=1]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are tasked with performing a data anonymization operation on a given user query. Your goal is to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) from the input while preserving the original meaning, intent, and structure of the query. The anonymization must be thorough, ensuring that no PII remains in the output, and all PII elements must be replaced with consistent, contextually appropriate generic placeholders.

### Task Description:
You will process a query and systematically identify and replace the following types of PII with placeholders:

1. **Individual Names** (e.g., "Jim", "Mrs. Dipert", "Troy Williams") → Use placeholder: `[Name]` or `[Recipient Name]` depending on context.
2. **Company or Organization Names** (e.g., "City of Arlington’s Office of Business Diversity", "CATL", "CHN ENERGY", "BYD", "GOTION HIGH-TECH", "Sunwoda Energy", "Envision") → Use placeholder: `[Company Name]`.
3. **Product or Technical Terms** (e.g., "engineering plastics", "PC", "PCABS", "PA12", "EVBP", "LEV", "ESS") → Use placeholder: `[Product Name]` or `[Technical Term]` depending on context.
4. **Customer Names** (e.g., "Customer A", "Client X") → Use placeholder: `[Customer Name]`.
5. **Locations or Cities** (e.g., "Arlington", "Shanghai") → Use placeholder: `[City Name]` or `[Location]`.
6. **Platform or System Names** (e.g., "Stan Store", "SAP") → Use placeholder: `[Platform Name]` or `[System Name]`.

### Important Rules and Guidelines:
- **Preserve the original structure** of the input, including formatting, line breaks, and markdown elements such as `<br/>` and numbered lists.
- **Use consistent placeholders** for similar types of PII. For example, always use `[Company Name]` for company names, not `[Organization Name]` unless the context clearly indicates a different entity.
- **Do not alter the meaning or intent** of the original query. Even if the query is a question or instruction, the anonymized version must reflect the same intent.
- **Be especially careful with technical or product-specific terms**, as they may be PII in the context of the query.
- **Avoid assumptions** about the user's intent beyond what is explicitly stated in the query.
- **Ensure no PII leakage** occurs in the output. This includes not only names and company names but also any other identifiers that could be used to trace the query back to a real-world entity or person.
- **Review the output for grammatical correctness and clarity**, ensuring that the placeholders do not disrupt the readability or coherence of the rewritten query.

### Examples of Proper Anonymization:
- Original: "How large is the SAP installation of Procter & Gamble?"
  - Rewritten: "How large is the [Platform Name] installation of [Company Name]?"
- Original: "If Jim puts in an order to purchase 30 shares of company A for $1.30 while the current price is $1.35, and the order is canceled immediately, what type of order did he put in?"
  - Rewritten: "If [Name] puts in an order to purchase 30 shares of [Company Name] for $1.30 while the current price is $1.35, and the order is canceled immediately, what type of order did he put in?"

### Final Review:
After generating the anonymized query, **review it carefully** to ensure:
- All PII has been replaced with placeholders.
- Placeholders are used consistently and appropriately.
- The query is grammatically correct and maintains the original intent.
- No PII remains in the output.

This task is crucial for **data anonymization, redaction, and privacy-preserving processing** in contexts such as customer support, compliance, and data analysis. Your output must be suitable for downstream processing or analysis that requires strict data privacy standards.

### Task Requirements:

1. **Identify and Replace PII Elements**:
   - **Names of individuals** (e.g., "Jim", "Troy Williams", "Mrs. Dipert") should be replaced with **[Name]** or **[Recipient Name]** depending on context.
